completes semantically while no visible object moved.\r\n\r\n## Category C: Animation runs poorly\r\n\r\nExamples:\r\n\r\n* abrupt,\r\n* too fast,\r\n* too slow,\r\n* visually weak,\r\n* generic fade,\r\n* disconnected from the physical object,\r\n* poor easing,\r\n* no anticipation,\r\n* no settle,\r\n* no secondary motion,\r\n* timing does not match sound,\r\n* animation begins before the section.\r\n\r\n## Category D: Animation only runs once\r\n\r\nDetermine whether each one-shot is:\r\n\r\n* intentionally ceremonial,\r\n* unintentionally blocked,\r\n* session-only,\r\n* tab-only,\r\n* device-only,\r\n* account-only,\r\n* campaign-only,\r\n* event-only,\r\n* replayable,\r\n* not replayable,\r\n* replayable only before refresh,\r\n* incorrectly replayed automatically.\r\n\r\nInspect:\r\n\r\n* `sessionStorage`,\r\n* `localStorage`,\r\n* component-local refs,\r\n* event acknowledgement,\r\n* sequence tracking,\r\n* route remount behavior,\r\n* React key behavior,\r\n* CSS animation iteration counts,\r\n* viewport `once` options,\r\n* persisted â€œseenâ€ flags.\r\n\r\n## Category E: Animation does not replay correctly\r\n\r\nExamples:\r\n\r\n* replay button disappears after refresh,\r\n* replay works only from the Journal,\r\n* replay mutates server state,\r\n* replay uses stale event data,\r\n* replay does not restore previous section,\r\n* replay leaves elements in a transformed state,\r\n* replay works once but fails a second time,\r\n* replay conflicts with a live event.\r\n\r\n## Category F: Wrong library owns the behavior\r\n\r\nFor every questionable animation, identify:\r\n\r\n* current owner,\r\n* correct owner,\r\n* reason,\r\n* migration recommendation,\r\n* wrappers or bridge required.\r\n\r\nExamples:\r\n\r\n* Motion and GSAP writing transform on the same node,\r\n* GSAP page-flip scenes duplicating StPageFlip,\r\n* CSS controlling narrative order,\r\n* Lottie autoplaying versus CSS transitions,\r\n* Motion layout versus StPageFlip,\r\n* Motion layoutId versus GSAP FLIP,\r\n* hidden PageFlip sources versus visible clones,\r\n* Rive container transforms versus external transforms,\r\n* Lottie containers moved by the wrong owner.\r\n\r\nIdentify every element with overlapping property writers.\r\n\r\n## Category H: Missing trigger\r\n\r\nExamples:\r\n\r\n* scene exists but has no event,\r\n* page turn occurs but no lifecycle scene is emitted,\r\n* inspection scene exists but opening the inspection never calls it,\r\n* ship-course exists but current position instance counts,\r\n* PageFlip instance leaks,\r\n* GSAP context reversion.\r\n\r\n## Category J: Reduced-motion defect\r\n\r\nAudit:\r\n\r\n* browser `prefers-reduced-motion`,\r\n* product full/gentle/reduced setting,\r\n* MotionConfig,\r\n* CSS media queries,\r\n* GSAP duration scaling,\r\n* PageFlip fallback,\r\n* Lottie representative frames,\r\n* Rive stable poses,\r\n* sound behavior,\r\n* keyboard and focus behavior.\r\n\r\nReduced mode must preserve narrative order and readable state without unnecessary spatial travel.\r\n\r\n## Category K: Performance problem\r\n\r\nAudit:\r\n\r\n* main-thread long tasks,\r\n* duplicate runtime mounting,\r\n* mode-change recreation,\r\n* unnecessary JSON reloads,\r\n* repeated layout reads,\r\n* FLIP layout thrashing,\r\n* excessive SVG nodes,\r\n* broad selectors,\r\n* hidden elements being animated,\r\n* large blur/filter costs,\r\n* mobile GPU pressure,\r\n* memory after repeated replay and navigation.\r\n\r\n## Category L: Animation is missing and should be added\r\n\r\nCreate a very large list of missing animation opportunities for every screen.\r\n\r\nEach recommendation must identify:\r\n\r\n* screen,\r\n* user action or event,\r\n* proposed animation,\r\n* correct library,\r\n* trigger,\r\n* replay policy,\r\n* reduced-motion alternative,\r\n* priority,\r\n* why it improves the experience.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 5. Baseline Findings That Must Be Verified\r\n\r\nThe following issues were identified during an external source audit. Treat these as high-priority hypotheses that must be independently verified against the exact commit.\r\n\r\nDo not blindly repeat them. Confirm, refine, disprove or expand them with code and runtime evidence.\r\n\r\n## 5.1 Production Rive assets may all be fallbacks\r\n\r\nVerify whether the following production contracts have actual `.riv` paths:\r\n\r\n* invitation seal,\r\n* journal clasp,\r\n* voyage compass,\r\n* finale mechanism.\r\n\r\nDetermine whether real product screens are receiving only static SVG fallback content.\r\n\r\nDocument the exact screens affected and whether the UI misleadingly appears to use Rive when it does not.\r\n\r\n## 5.2 New platform sign-in pages may bypass cinematic authentication\r\n\r\nCompare:\r\n\r\n* modern Player sign-in,\r\n* modern Captain/Creator sign-in,\r\n* legacy Player AccessGate,\r\n* legacy Quartermaster login.\r\n\r\nDetermine which flows call AnimationDirector and which perform direct fetch-and-route behavior.\r\n\r\n## 5.3 Invitation Ceremony may currently be a static form\r\n\r\nVerify whether invitation acceptance, decline, PIN validation, invalid state, expiration and route transitions use any of:\r\n\r\n* GSAP,\r\n* Motion,\r\n* Rive,\r\n* Lottie,\r\n* CSS state sequences.\r\n\r\n## 5.4 Registered scenes may exist only in the showcase\r\n\r\nInvestigate these scenes:\r\n\r\n* `journal-open`\r\n* `manual-page-flip`\r\n* `programmatic-page-flip`\r\n* `chapter-heading`\r\n* `prose-ink`\r\n* `seal-break`\r\n* `marker-stamp`\r\n* `ship-course`\r\n* `artifact-inspection`\r\n\r\nFor each, document all real product call sites.\r\n\r\nIf there are none, mark the scene as dead, showcase-only, legacy-only or future-contract-only.\r\n\r\n## 5.5 Chapter release may be invisible outside the Journal\r\n\r\nVerify what happens when `CHAPTER_RELEASED` arrives while the Player is viewing:\r\n\r\n* Chart,\r\n* Treasures,\r\n* Quests,\r\n* Log,\r\n* Finale.\r\n\r\nThe chapter ceremony content appears to be mounted only inside JournalWorkspace.\r\n\r\nTest whether the scene:\r\n\r\n* animates nothing,\r\n* animates unrelated background targets,\r\n* remains invisible,\r\n* moves the user to Journal,\r\n* or uses a global overlay.\r\n\r\n## 5.6 Ceremony replay may fail outside Journal\r\n\r\nTest Replay Ceremony while each Player section is active.\r\n\r\nAlso test replay:\r\n\r\n* immediately,\r\n* twice in succession,\r\n* after route navigation,\r\n* after browser refresh,\r\n* after motion-mode change,\r\n* during another live event.\r\n\r\n## 5.7 Replay state may disappear after refresh\r\n\r\nVerify whether `lastRelease` or equivalent replay information is reconstructed from a safe server snapshot or exists only in component memory.\r\n\r\n## 5.8 Generic scene-part names may animate duplicates\r\n\r\nSearch for duplicate use of:\r\n\r\n* `route-path`\r\n* `map-fog`\r\n* `map-marker-new`\r\n* `artifact-reveal`\r\n* `artifact-light`\r\n* `artifact-slot-target`\r\n* `artifact-connection-path`\r\n* `quest-note-new`\r\n* `quest-stamp`\r\n* `red-thread`\r\n* `log-entry-new`\r\n* `log-symbol-new`\r\n* `finale-ring-outer`\r\n* `finale-ring-inner`\r\n* `finale-light-path`\r\n* `workspace-light`\r\n* `lantern`\r\n* `peripheral`\r\n\r\nDetermine whether a single scene animates:\r\n\r\n* a permanent screen target,\r\n* a temporary event overlay,\r\n* hidden source content,\r\n* and visible clones simultaneously.\r\n\r\n## 5.9 PageFlip source nodes may receive GSAP animation\r\n\r\nInspect the hidden React source used by `PageFlipBook` and the cloned visible StPageFlip DOM.\r\n\r\nDetermine whether animation attributes survive into both trees and whether GSAP can animate the hidden source instead of the visible page.\r\n\r\n## 5.10 Ownership may be warning-only\r\n\r\nVerify whether a rejected animation ownership claim actually prevents the animation from running.\r\n\r\nAudit whether Motion elements register ownership in the same runtime registry or merely include a data attribute.\r\n\r\n## 5.11 Confirm Motion and GSAP transform conflicts\r\n\r\nSpecifically inspect:\r\n\r\n* Voyage Chart marker buttons,\r\n* Shipâ€™s Log entries,\r\n* artifact inspection shared-layout object,\r\n* companion navigation,\r\n* Quartermaster action buttons,\r\n* any element with both Motion layout/layoutId and `data-gsap-owned`.\r\n\r\n## 5.12 PageFlip motion mode may not update correctly\r\n\r\nVerify whether changing from full to gentle mode updates `flippingTime` on an existing PageFlip instance.\r\n\r\nInspect effect dependencies and runtime recreation.\r\n\r\n## 5.13 Lottie may reload on every mode change\r\n\r\nVerify whether changing full/gentle/reduced:\r\n\r\n* destroys the runtime,\r\n* reloads JSON,\r\n* restarts ambient loops,\r\n* replays non-looping ink effects,\r\n* creates visible blank frames.\r\n\r\n## 5.14 CSS phase waiting may hang\r\n\r\nInspect `waitForJournalPhase()`.\r\n\r\nTest:\r\n\r\n* abort during a phase,\r\n* infinite animation under an actor,\r\n* browser animation promise that never resolves,\r\n* missing actor,\r\n* missing transition,\r\n* reduced mode,\r\n* unmount during wait.\r\n\r\n## 5.15 Empty target arrays may silently pass\r\n\r\nDetermine which GSAP scenes can progress through all labels with no required visible targets.\r\n\r\nAdd evidence for scenes that â€œcompleteâ€ without moving anything.\r\n\r\n## 5.16 GSAP cleanup may cause final-state snapback\r\n\r\nTest access/login success and route-changing sequences.\r\n\r\nDetermine whether GSAP context reversion restores the closed seal, door or lock before navigation completes.\r\n\r\n## 5.17 Reduced-motion behavior may have multiple competing authorities\r\n\r\nInspect:\r\n\r\n* custom motion mode,\r\n* browser preference,\r\n* MotionConfig,\r\n* CSS media query,\r\n* PageFlip reduced fallback,\r\n* Lottie mode behavior,\r\n* Rive autoplay.\r\n\r\nDetermine whether any Motion component can still animate spatially under browser reduced motion because it forgot to consume the custom mode.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 6. Required Investigation Method\r\n\r\n## 6.1 Static source inventory\r\n\r\nSearch the entire source tree for:\r\n\r\n```text\r\ngsap\r\nuseGSAP\r\ndirector.play\r\nmotion.\r\n<motion\r\nAnimatePresence\r\nlayoutId\r\nlayout\r\nwhileHover\r\nwhileTap\r\npage-flip\r\nPageFlipBook\r\nRiveStatefulObject\r\nuseRive\r\nLottieEffect\r\nlottie-web\r\n@keyframes\r\nanimation:\r\ntransition:\r\ngetAnimations\r\nsessionStorage\r\nlocalStorage\r\nprefers-reduced-motion\r\nrequestAnimationFrame\r\nsetTimeout\r\nsetInterval\r\ndata-scene-part\r\ndata-gsap-owned\r\ndata-animation-owner\r\ndata-opening-actor\r\ndata-journal-phase\r\ndata-cinematic\r\n```\r\n\r\nCreate a complete inventory of:\r\n\r\n* animation files,\r\n* animation call sites,\r\n* scene definitions,\r\n* scene consumers,\r\n* animation assets,\r\n* CSS keyframes,\r\n* transition-based state machines,\r\n* replay flags,\r\n* one-shot flags,\r\n* fallback paths,\r\n* test coverage.\r\n\r\n## 6.2 Scene reachability graph\r\n\r\nFor every registered scene, produce:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nScene name\r\nDefinition file\r\nReal production call sites\r\nDevelopment-only call sites\r\nRequired targets\r\nOptional targets\r\nCurrent root scope\r\nTriggering event/action\r\nReplay path\r\nReduced behavior\r\nKnown conflicts\r\nReachability status\r\n```\r\n\r\nReachability status must be one of:\r\n\r\n* Production active\r\n* Legacy active\r\n* Development showcase only\r\n* Registered but unreachable\r\n* Partially integrated\r\n* Fallback-only\r\n* Dead or redundant\r\n* Unknown pending runtime test\r\n\r\n## 6.3 Live browser testing\r\n\r\nWhere possible, run the real application on port 3000 and test with browser automation and manual inspection.\r\n\r\nDo not rely solely on unit tests.\r\n\r\nCapture evidence at meaningful states, not arbitrary delays.\r\n\r\nTest at minimum:\r\n\r\n* 2560 Ã— 1440\r\n* 1920 Ã— 1080\r\n* 1440 Ã— 900\r\n* 430 Ã— 932\r\n* 390 Ã— 844\r\n* 844 Ã— 390\r\n\r\nTest:\r\n\r\n* full motion,\r\n* gentle motion,\r\n* product reduced motion,\r\n* browser reduced motion,\r\n* sound enabled,\r\n* sound disabled,\r\n* cached assets,\r\n* uncached assets,\r\n* first visit,\r\n* return visit,\r\n* refresh,\r\n* back/forward navigation,\r\n* replay,\r\n* skip,\r\n* failed requests,\r\n* slow requests,\r\n* offline/reconnect,\r\n* route unmount during animation.\r\n\r\nUse screenshots, Playwright traces, console output and performance evidence where appropriate.\r\n\r\nStore temporary evidence under an ignored audit directory such as:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nartifacts/animation-audit/\r\n```\r\n\r\nDo not commit large generated traces or screenshots unless explicitly required by repository documentation policy.\r\n\r\n## 6.4 Visible-target verification\r\n\r\nFor each cinematic scene, record at runtime:\r\n\r\n* required target count,\r\n* optional target count,\r\n* visible target count,\r\n* duplicate target count,\r\n* target bounding boxes,\r\n* target opacity,\r\n* target display/visibility state,\r\n* current Player section,\r\n* scene instance ID,\r\n* animation owner,\r\n* actual properties animated.\r\n\r\nA scene must not be considered visually successful merely because its timeline completed.\r\n\r\n## 6.5 Replay testing\r\n\r\nFor every replayable scene:\r\n\r\n1. Play once.\r\n2. Replay immediately.\r\n3. Replay again.\r\n4. Navigate away and replay.\r\n5. Refresh and replay.\r\n6. Switch motion mode and replay.\r\n7. Skip midway and replay.\r\n8. Interrupt with another scene.\r\n9. Verify no server mutation occurred.\r\n10. Verify cleanup returned all runtime counts to expected values.\r\n\r\n## 6.6 One-shot analysis\r\n\r\nFor every animation that does not automatically repeat, determine exactly why.\r\n\r\nDo not write vague statements such as â€œruns once.â€\r\n\r\nWrite:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nRuns once per:\r\n- component mount\r\n- browser tab\r\n- sessionStorage key\r\n- device\r\n- campaign\r\n- acknowledged event\r\n- route visit\r\n- application session\r\n```\r\n\r\nAlso document whether that policy is correct.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 7. Required Per-Animation Matrix\r\n\r\nCreate a master matrix with one row per animation, effect, transition or missing opportunity.\r\n\r\nThe matrix must include at least these fields:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nID\r\nScreen\r\nRole\r\nComponent\r\nAnimation or proposed animation\r\nCurrent library\r\nCorrect library\r\nCurrent trigger\r\nExpected trigger\r\nCurrent replay policy\r\nRecommended replay policy\r\nRuns at all?\r\nVisible when run?\r\nRuns only once?\r\nWorks after refresh?\r\nWorks from every relevant section?\r\nFull mode result\r\nGentle mode result\r\nReduced mode result\r\nMobile result\r\nDesktop result\r\nRequired targets\r\nMissing targets\r\nDuplicate targets\r\nOwnership conflicts\r\nCleanup status\r\nFallback status\r\nPerformance concerns\r\nAccessibility concerns\r\nCurrent quality\r\nFailure severity\r\nRecommended change\r\nImplementation complexity\r\nImplementation priority\r\nTest coverage\r\nEvidence\r\nSource files\r\n```\r\n\r\nThe final matrix should be large. Do not impose an artificial item limit.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 8. Required Per-Library Audit\r\n\r\n## 8.1 GSAP audit\r\n\r\nDocument:\r\n\r\n* every scene,\r\n* every call site,\r\n* every selector,\r\n* every required target,\r\n* every optional target,\r\n* every empty-target possibility,\r\n* every global-root problem,\r\n* every cleanup/reversion issue,\r\n* every skip issue,\r\n* every failure branch,\r\n* every success branch,\r\n* every idle loop,\r\n* every reversible scene,\r\n* every timeline that can visually snap back,\r\n* every scene that should be split or retired.\r\n\r\nRecommend:\r\n\r\n* dedicated scene hosts,\r\n* scene instance IDs,\r\n* required-target contracts,\r\n* playback policies,\r\n* final-state policies,\r\n* interruption priorities,\r\n* semantic audio labels,\r\n* runtime visual assertions.\r\n\r\n## 8.2 Motion audit\r\n\r\nDocument:\r\n\r\n* all presence transitions,\r\n* layout transitions,\r\n* shared-layout transitions,\r\n* buttons and press effects,\r\n* dialogs,\r\n* cards,\r\n* tabs,\r\n* filters,\r\n* list updates,\r\n* section navigation,\r\n* all missing Motion opportunities in the modern platform.\r\n\r\nFind every node where Motion and GSAP may both write:\r\n\r\n* transform,\r\n* opacity,\r\n* layout,\r\n* scale,\r\n* x/y,\r\n* clip path.\r\n\r\nRecommend wrapper separation.\r\n\r\n## 8.3 StPageFlip audit\r\n\r\nDocument:\r\n\r\n* initialization,\r\n* mode changes,\r\n* page updates,\r\n* orientation,\r\n* keyboard handling,\r\n* pending turn queue,\r\n* source cloning,\r\n* visible DOM,\r\n* hidden source DOM,\r\n* failure fallback,\r\n* reduced mode,\r\n* cleanup,\r\n* page preservation,\r\n* filter-induced recreation,\r\n* responsive behavior.\r\n\r\nDetermine whether manual/programmatic GSAP page-flip scenes should be removed.\r\n\r\n## 8.4 Rive audit\r\n\r\nDocument:\r\n\r\n* every contract,\r\n* every real `.riv` asset,\r\n* every fallback,\r\n* every state machine,\r\n* every input,\r\n* every screen,\r\n* production versus development behavior.\r\n\r\nCreate a detailed specification for missing project-authored Rive assets:\r\n\r\n* Invitation Seal\r\n* Journal Clasp\r\n* Voyage Compass\r\n* Finale Mechanism\r\n\r\nInclude required states, inputs, transitions and reduced-motion poses.\r\n\r\n## 8.5 Lottie audit\r\n\r\nDocument:\r\n\r\n* every JSON asset,\r\n* every mount,\r\n* autoplay,\r\n* loop,\r\n* speed,\r\n* visibility pause,\r\n* document pause,\r\n* mode changes,\r\n* failure handling,\r\n* stalled-load handling,\r\n* timing relative to GSAP scenes.\r\n\r\nIdentify non-looping Lottie effects that begin before their intended semantic scene label.\r\n\r\n## 8.6 CSS audit\r\n\r\nInventory:\r\n\r\n* all keyframes,\r\n* all long transitions,\r\n* data-attribute state machines,\r\n* journal opening mechanics,\r\n* waiting-room breathing,\r\n* ambient effects,\r\n* focus/hover transitions,\r\n* reduced-motion overrides.\r\n\r\nSeparate:\r\n\r\n* material rendering,\r\n* ambient animation,\r\n* narrative orchestration.\r\n\r\nRecommend moving narrative ordering out of CSS without removing CSS material behavior.\r\n\r\n## 8.7 Web Animations API audit\r\n\r\nAudit:\r\n\r\n* use of `getAnimations`,\r\n* handling of `animation.finished`,\r\n* abort,\r\n* timeout,\r\n* infinite animations,\r\n* missing animation detection,\r\n* expected actor validation.\r\n\r\n## 8.8 Audio audit\r\n\r\nMap every sound cue to:\r\n\r\n* current trigger,\r\n* desired semantic label,\r\n* timing offset,\r\n* missing visual synchronization,\r\n* reduced/silent behavior.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 9. Required Missing-Animation Blueprint\r\n\r\nThe final report must include a massive list of animations that should be added.\r\n\r\nDo not merely list names. For each proposed addition include:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nScreen\r\nMoment\r\nUser benefit\r\nVisual concept\r\nCorrect library\r\nSupporting library if any\r\nTrigger\r\nDuration range\r\nReplay policy\r\nReduced-motion behavior\r\nSound cue\r\nFailure fallback\r\nPriority\r\n```\r\n\r\nInclude additions for at least:\r\n\r\n* Landing and role selection\r\n* Player sign-in\r\n* Captain sign-in\r\n* Creator sign-in\r\n* Invitation ceremony\r\n* Player Library\r\n* Captain Library\r\n* New Voyage wizard\r\n* Waiting room\r\n* Journal opening\r\n* Journal pages\r\n* Chapter release\r\n* Chart\r\n* Treasure Altar\r\n* Artifact inspection\r\n* Side quests\r\n* Shipâ€™s Log\r\n* Finale\r\n* Quartermaster commands\r\n* Studio authoring\r\n* loading/error/success states\r\n* shell navigation\r\n* route transitions\r\n* theme/color-scheme transitions\r\n* offline/reconnect\r\n* notification and unseen-content states\r\n\r\nDo not reduce the list to ten or twenty items. The goal is a comprehensive experience blueprint.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 10. Required Deliverables\r\n\r\nCreate the following files inside `Development_Docs`:\r\n\r\n## 10.1 Master audit\r\n\r\n```text\r\nDevelopment_Docs/Animation_System_Full_Audit.md\r\n```\r\n\r\nThis must contain:\r\n\r\n1. Executive summary\r\n2. Audit baseline and methodology\r\n3. Current architecture\r\n4. Current library inventory\r\n5. Scene reachability report\r\n6. Animations that do not run\r\n7. Animations that run invisibly\r\n8. Animations that run poorly\r\n9. One-shot and replay analysis\r\n10. Ownership conflicts\r\n11. Wrong-library findings\r\n12. Lifecycle and cleanup findings\r\n13. Reduced-motion findings\r\n14. Performance findings\r\n15. Per-screen audit\r\n16. Per-library audit\r\n17. Massive missing-animation list\r\n18. Recommended architecture\r\n19. Severity-ranked findings\r\n20. Evidence references\r\n21. Limitations and items requiring further runtime confirmation\r\n\r\n## 10.2 Detailed animation matrix\r\n\r\n```text\r\nDevelopment_Docs/Animation_System_Audit_Matrix.csv\r\n```\r\n\r\nThe CSV must be genuinely useful for implementation planning and must contain the required fields specified earlier.\r\n\r\nDo not create a CSV containing vague one-line summaries.\r\n\r\n## 10.3 Implementation roadmap\r\n\r\n```text\r\nDevelopment_Docs/Animation_System_Implementation_Roadmap.md\r\n```\r\n\r\nOrganize implementation into no more than six major phases.\r\n\r\nA recommended phase structure is:\r\n\r\n1. **Animation truth and broken-trigger repair**\r\n2. **Ownership and scene-scoping architecture**\r\n3. **Player cinematic integration**\r\n4. **Platform, Library and Invitation motion**\r\n5. **Rive/Lottie/PageFlip completion**\r\n6. **Performance, accessibility and final polish**\r\n\r\nFor each phase include:\r\n\r\n* exact scope,\r\n* dependencies,\r\n* files likely affected,\r\n* libraries involved,\r\n* acceptance criteria,\r\n* tests,\r\n* risks,\r\n* work that can happen in parallel,\r\n* work that must not happen in parallel.\r\n\r\n## 10.4 Animation test plan\r\n\r\n```text\r\nDevelopment_Docs/Animation_System_Test_Plan.md\r\n```\r\n\r\nInclude:\r\n\r\n* unit tests,\r\n* component tests,\r\n* end-to-end tests,\r\n* visual checkpoint tests,\r\n* target-integrity tests,\r\n* replay tests,\r\n* one-shot tests,\r\n* every-event/every-section matrix,\r\n* mode matrix,\r\n* viewport matrix,\r\n* interruption tests,\r\n* performance tests,\r\n* memory-leak tests,\r\n* fallback tests.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 11. Severity and Priority Rules\r\n\r\nUse these severity levels:\r\n\r\n## P0 - Broken core experience\r\n\r\nExamples:\r\n\r\n* a major ceremony is invisible,\r\n* animation blocks interaction indefinitely,\r\n* route cannot complete,\r\n* reduced-motion accessibility failure,\r\n* production asset silently does not exist,\r\n* server event is acknowledged despite no visible required presentation when presentation is mandatory.\r\n\r\n## P1 - Major quality or consistency failure\r\n\r\nExamples:\r\n\r\n* wrong object animates,\r\n* duplicate objects animate,\r\n* replay is unavailable,\r\n* animation differs unpredictably by section,\r\n* severe library ownership collision,\r\n* visible snapback,\r\n* page-turn setting does not apply.\r\n\r\n## P2 - Noticeable polish deficiency\r\n\r\nExamples:\r\n\r\n* weak easing,\r\n* generic fade,\r\n* missing secondary motion,\r\n* missing form transition,\r\n* poor loading state,\r\n* abrupt filtering.\r\n\r\n## P3 - Enhancement\r\n\r\nExamples:\r\n\r\n* richer ambient motion,\r\n* optional parallax,\r\n* subtle hover refinement,\r\n* additional material response.\r\n\r\nPrioritize correctness and consistency before adding decorative layers.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 12. Required Final Recommendations\r\n\r\nThe final audit must answer all of the following:\r\n\r\n1. Which animations are completely broken?\r\n2. Which animations do not run in production?\r\n3. Which animations run only in the development showcase?\r\n4. Which animations run but target invisible elements?\r\n5. Which animations depend on the Playerâ€™s current section?\r\n6. Which animations run once?\r\n7. Which one-shot policies are correct?\r\n8. Which one-shot policies should change?\r\n9. Which animations cannot replay after refresh?\r\n10. Which scenes have no real trigger?\r\n11. Which scenes should be retired?\r\n12. Which scenes should be connected?\r\n13. Which behaviors use the wrong library?\r\n14. Which nodes have conflicting owners?\r\n15. Which Rive objects are currently static fallbacks?\r\n16. Which Lottie effects restart incorrectly?\r\n17. Which PageFlip behaviors fail after mode changes?\r\n18. Which CSS phase waits can hang or skip?\r\n19. Which animations are missing from modern platform screens?\r\n20. What should be added to make the entire experience feel unified and premium?\r\n21. What exact implementation sequence should follow?\r\n22. Which work can be done in parallel?\r\n23. What automated tests are required before declaring the animation system complete?\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 13. Hard Boundaries\r\n\r\nDo not:\r\n\r\n* broadly implement fixes during this audit,\r\n* rewrite the entire animation architecture,\r\n* replace all libraries with GSAP,\r\n* replace all libraries with Motion,\r\n* delete Rive because final assets are missing,\r\n* replace StPageFlip with a homegrown book animation,\r\n* change unrelated product functionality,\r\n* alter narrative or personal content,\r\n* expose private content,\r\n* interfere with concurrent animation-fix work,\r\n* stage the entire repository,\r\n* claim runtime confirmation without actually running the relevant flow,\r\n* claim an animation works merely because a timeline completed,\r\n* claim a fallback is a real Rive animation,\r\n* produce only a short summary.\r\n\r\nTemporary non-invasive instrumentation is acceptable if required for investigation, but it must either:\r\n\r\n* remain isolated and clearly documented, or\r\n* be reverted before task completion.\r\n\r\nThe final committed application source should remain unchanged unless there is an extremely small audit-support correction that is separately justified. Documentation files are the intended output.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 14. Quality Bar\r\n\r\nThe audit is complete only when:\r\n\r\n* every registered scene has a reachability status,\r\n* every real animation call site has been inventoried,\r\n* every production animation library has a status,\r\n* all known hypotheses have been verified or disproved,\r\n* one-shot and replay behavior is documented per animation,\r\n* broken and invisible animation paths are identified,\r\n* ownership conflicts are mapped,\r\n* the modern platform and legacy cinematic paths are compared,\r\n* every major screen has a missing-animation blueprint,\r\n* the audit matrix is extensive,\r\n* the implementation roadmap is actionable,\r\n* and the test plan would prevent the same regressions from returning.\r\n\r\nThe result should be detailed enough that future Codex implementation prompts can use the audit as the governing source of truth and implement one phase at a time without guessing.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 15. Include `isDraft=false` for ready PRs.\n- Only emit these git directives in your final response after the action actually succeeds, never in commentary updates. Keep attributes single-line.\n</app-context>\r\n<collaboration_mode># Collaboration Mode: Default\r\n\r\nYou are now in Default mode. Editing files in other directories requires approval. Network access is enabled.\n# Escalation Requests\r\n\r\nCommands are run outside the sandbox if they are approved by the user, or match an existing rule that allows it to run unrestricted. The command string is split into independent command segments at shell control operators, including but not limited to:\r\n\r\n- Pipes: |\r\n- Logical operators: &&, ||\r\n- Command separators: ;\r\n- Subshell boundaries: (...), $(...)\r\n\r\nEach resulting segment is evaluated independently for sandbox restrictions and approval requirements.\r\n\r\nExample:\r\n\r\ngit pull | tee output.txt\r\n\r\nThis is treated as two command segments:\r\n\r\n[\"git\", \"pull\"]\r\n\r\n[\"tee\", \"output.txt\"]\r\n\r\nCommands that use more advanced shell features like redirection (>, >>, <), substitutions ($(...), ...), environment variables (FOO=bar), or wildcard patterns (*, ?) will not be evaluated against rules, to limit the scope of what an approved rule allows.\r\n\r\n## How to request escalation\r\n\r\nIMPORTANT: To request approval to execute a command that will require escalated privileges:\r\n\r\n- Provide the `sandbox_permissions` parameter with the value `\"require_escalated\"`\r\n- Include a short question asking the user if they want to allow the action in `justification` parameter. e.g. \"Do you want to download and install dependencies for this project?\"\r\n- Optionally suggest a `prefix_rule` - this will be shown to the user with an option to persist the rule approval for future sessions.\r\n\r\nIf you run a command that is important to solving the user's query, but it fails because of sandboxing or with a likely sandbox-related network error (for example DNS/host resolution, registry/index access, or dependency download failure), rerun the command with \"require_escalated\". ALWAYS proceed to use the `justification` parameter - do not message the user before requesting approval for the command.\r\n\r\n## When to request escalation\r\n\r\nWhile commands are running inside the sandbox, here are some scenarios that will require escalation outside the sandbox:\r\n\r\n- You need to run a command that writes to a directory that requires it (e.g. running tests that write to /var)\r\n- You need to run a GUI app (e.g., open/xdg-open/osascript) to open browsers or files.\r\n- If you run a command that is important to solving the user's query, but it fails because of sandboxing or with a likely sandbox-related network error (for example DNS/host resolution, registry/index access, or dependency download failure), rerun the command with `require_escalated`. ALWAYS proceed to use the `sandbox_permissions` and `justification` parameters. do not message the user before requesting approval for the command.\r\n- You are about to take a potentially destructive action such as an `rm` or `git reset` that the user did not explicitly ask for.\r\n- Be judicious with escalating, but if completing the user's request requires it, you should do so - don't try and circumvent approvals by using other tools.\r\n\r\n## prefix_rule guidance\r\n\r\nWhen choosing a `prefix_rule`, request one that will allow you to fulfill similar requests from the user in the future without re-requesting escalation. It should be categorical and reasonably scoped to similar capabilities. You should rarely pass the entire command into `prefix_rule`.\r\n\r\n### Banned prefix_rules \r\nAvoid requesting overly broad prefixes that the user would be ill-advised to approve. For example, do not request [\"python3\"], [\"python\", \"-\"], or other similar prefixes that would allow arbitrary scripting.\r\nNEVER provide a prefix_rule argument for destructive commands like rm.\r\nNEVER provide a prefix_rule if your command uses a heredoc or herestring. \r\n\r\n### Examples\r\nGood examples of prefixes:\r\n- [\"npm\", \"run\", \"dev\"]\r\n- [\"gh\", \"pr\", \"check\"]\r\n- [\"cargo\", \"test\"]\r\n The writable roots are `C:\\Users\\kkids\\.codex\\visualizations\\2026\\07\\18\\019f7612-5f0c-7941-8ee5-cf9390e1a6ea`, `C:\\Users\\kkids\\Documents\\Codex_TreasureHunt`.\n</permissions instructions>\r\n\n===== MESSAGE 16 role=user status= =====\r\n<environment_context>\n  <current_date>2026-07-18</current_date>\n  <timezone>America/New_York</timezone>\n  <filesystem><workspace_roots><root>C:\\Users\\kkids\\Documents\\Codex_TreasureHunt</root></workspace_roots><permission_profile type=\"managed\"><file_system type=\"restricted\"><entry access=\"read\"><special>:root</special></entry><entry access=\"write\"><path>C:\\Users\\kkids\\Documents\\Codex_TreasureHunt</path></entry><entry access=\"write\"><special>:slash_tmp</special></entry><entry access=\"write\"><special>:tmpdir</special></entry><entry access=\"write\"><path>C:\\Users\\kkids\\.codex\\visualizations\\2026\\07\\18\\019f7612-5f0c-7941-8ee5-cf9390e1a6ea</path></entry><entry access=\"read\"><path>C:\\Users\\kkids\\Documents\\Codex_TreasureHunt\\.git</path></entry><entry access=\"read\"><path>C:\\Users\\kkids\\Documents\\Codex_TreasureHunt\\.agents</path></entry><entry access=\"read\"><path>C:\\Users\\kkids\\Documents\\Codex_TreasureHunt\\.codex</path></entry></file_system></permission_profile></filesystem>\n</environment_context>\r\n\n===== MESSAGE 17 role=developer status= =====\r\n<skills_instructions>\n## Skills\nA skill is a set of instructions provided through a `SKILL.md` source. Severity and Priority Rules\\r\\n\\r\\nUse these severity levels:\\r\\n\\r\\n## P0 - Broken core experience\\r\\n\\r\\nExamples:\\r\\n\\r\\n* a major ceremony is invisible,\\r\\n* animation blocks interaction indefinitely,\\r\\n* route cannot complete,\\r\\n* reduced-motion accessibility failure,\\r\\n* production asset silently does not exist,\\r\\n* server event is acknowledged despite no visible required presentation when presentation is mandatory.\\r\\n\\r\\n## P1 - Major quality or consistency failure\\r\\n\\r\\nExamples:\\r\\n\\r\\n* wrong object animates,\\r\\n* duplicate objects animate,\\r\\n* replay is unavailable,\\r\\n* animation differs unpredictably by section,\\r\\n* severe library ownership collision,\\r\\n* visible snapback,\\r\\n* page-turn setting does not apply.\\r\\n\\r\\n## P2 - Noticeable polish deficiency\\r\\n\\r\\nExamples:\\r\\n\\r\\n* weak easing,\\r\\n* generic fade,\\r\\n* missing secondary motion,\\r\\n* missing form transition,\\r\\n* poor loading state,\\r\\n* abrupt filtering.\\r\\n\\r\\n## P3 - Enhancement\\r\\n\\r\\nExamples:\\r\\n\\r\\n* richer ambient motion,\\r\\n* optional parallax,\\r\\n* subtle hover refinement,\\r\\n* additional material response.\\r\\n\\r\\nPrioritize correctness and consistency before adding decorative layers.\\r\\n\\r\\n---\\r\\n\\r\\n# 12. Required Final Recommendations\\r\\n\\r\\nThe final audit must answer all of the following:\\r\\n\\r\\n1. Which animations are completely broken?\\r\\n2. Which animations do not run in production?\\r\\n3. Which animations run only in the development showcase?\\r\\n4. Which animations run but target invisible elements?\\r\\n5. Which animations depend on the Playerâ€™s current section?\\r\\n6. Which animations run once?\\r\\n7. Which one-shot policies are correct?\\r\\n8. Which one-shot policies should change?\\r\\n9.
